For the company, see <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Inc._(2017%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Yahoo! Inc. (2017–present)">Yahoo! Inc. (2017–present)</a>. For the now-unaffiliated Japanese company, see <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_Japan" title="Yahoo Japan">Yahoo Japan</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Yahoo (disambiguation)">Yahoo (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

services">List of products</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Revenue" title="Revenue">Revenue</a></th><td class="infobox-data">$7.4 billion (2020)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" <p><b>Yahoo</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/j/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;yes&#39;">j</span><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span><span title="&#39;h&#39; in &#39;hi&#39;">h</span><span title="/uː/: &#39;oo&#39; in &#39;goose&#39;">uː</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="ext-phonos"><span data-nosnippet="" id="ooui-php-1" class="noexcerpt ext-phonos-PhonosButton ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-buttonElement oo-ui-buttonElement-frameless oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-buttonWidget" data-ooui="{&quot;_&quot;:&quot;mw.Phonos.PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;href&quot;:&quot;\/\/upload.wikimedia.org\/wikipedia\/commons\/transcoded\/b\/b7\/En-us-yahoo.oga\/En-us-yahoo.oga.mp3&quot;,&quot;rel&quot;:[&quot;nofollow&quot;],&quot;framed&quot;:false,&quot;icon&quot;:&quot;volumeUp&quot;,&quot;data&quot;:{&quot;ipa&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;lang&quot;:&quot;en&quot;,&quot;wikibase&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;file&quot;:&quot;En-us-yahoo.oga&quot;},&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;noexcerpt&quot;,&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel&quot;]}"><a role="button" tabindex="0" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/b/b7/En-us-yahoo.oga/En-us-yahoo.oga.mp3" rel="nofollow" aria-label="Play audio" title="Play audio" class="oo-ui-buttonElement-button"><span class="oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-volumeUp"></span><span class="oo-ui-labelElement-label"></span><span class="oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicatorElement-noIndicator"></span></a></span><sup class="ext-phonos-attribution noexcerpt navigation-not-searchable"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-yahoo.oga" title="File:En-us-yahoo.oga">ⓘ</a></sup></span></span>, styled <b>yahoo<i>!</i></b> in its <a href="/wiki/Logo" title="Logo">logo</a>)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is an American <a href="/wiki/Web_portal" title="Web portal">web portal</a> that provides the search engine <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_Search" title="Yahoo Search">Yahoo Search</a> and related services including <a href="/wiki/My_Yahoo" title="My Yahoo">My Yahoo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_Mail" title="Yahoo Mail">Yahoo Mail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_News" title="Yahoo News">Yahoo News</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_Finance" title="Yahoo Finance">Yahoo Finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_Sports" title="Yahoo Sports">Yahoo Sports</a>, y!entertainment, yahoo!life,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and its advertising platform, <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_Native" title="Yahoo Native">Yahoo Native</a>. It is operated by the namesake company <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Inc._(2017%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Yahoo! Inc. (2017–present)">Yahoo! Inc.</a>, which is 90% owned by <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Global_Management" title="Apollo Global Management">Apollo Global Management</a> and 10% by <a href="/wiki/Verizon" title="Verizon">Verizon</a>.
</p><p>Yahoo was established by <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Yang" title="Jerry Yang">Jerry Yang</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Filo" title="David Filo">David Filo</a> in January 1994 and was one of the pioneers of the early Internet era in the 1990s.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, its use declined in the 2010s as some of its services were discontinued, and it lost market share to <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> and <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-telegraph.co.uk&#95;7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Etymology">Etymology</h2></div>
<p>The word "yahoo" is a <a href="/wiki/Backronym" title="Backronym">backronym</a> for "<a href="/wiki/Yet_another" title="Yet another">Yet Another</a> Hierarchically Organized Oracle"<sup id="cite&#95;ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or "Yet Another Hierarchical Officious Oracle".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The term "hierarchical" described how the Yahoo database was arranged in layers of subcategories. The term "oracle" was intended to mean "source of truth and wisdom", and the term "officious", rather than being related to the word's normal meaning, described the many office workers who would use the Yahoo database while surfing from work.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, founders Filo and Yang insist they mainly selected the name because they liked the slang definition of a "yahoo" (used by college students in David Filo's native Louisiana in the late 1980s and early 1990s to refer to an unsophisticated, rural Southerner): "rude, unsophisticated, uncouth."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This meaning derives from the <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_(Gulliver%27s_Travels)" title="Yahoo (Gulliver&#39;s Travels)">Yahoo</a> race of fictional beings from <i><a href="/wiki/Gulliver%27s_Travels" title="Gulliver&#39;s Travels">Gulliver's Travels</a></i>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Yahoo" title="History of Yahoo">History of Yahoo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Inc._(1995%E2%80%932017)" title="Yahoo! Inc. (1995–2017)">Yahoo! Inc. (1995–2017)</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Founding">Founding</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Jerry_Yang_and_David_Filo.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Jerry_Yang_and_David_Filo.jpg/250px-Jerry_Yang_and_David_Filo.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Jerry_Yang_and_David_Filo.jpg/500px-Jerry_Yang_and_David_Filo.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="899" data-file-height="677" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Jerry_Yang" title="Jerry Yang">Jerry Yang</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Filo" title="David Filo">David Filo</a>, the founders of Yahoo</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo_screenshot_1994.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/34/Yahoo_screenshot_1994.png/250px-Yahoo_screenshot_1994.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="218" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/34/Yahoo_screenshot_1994.png 1.5x" data-file-width="324" data-file-height="282" /></a><figcaption>The Yahoo home page in 1994, when it was a directory. A <a href="/wiki/Search_engine" title="Search engine">search engine</a> was added in 1995.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In January 1994, <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Yang" title="Jerry Yang">Jerry Yang</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Filo" title="David Filo">David Filo</a> were electrical engineering graduate students at <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>, when they created a website named "Jerry and David's guide to the World Wide Web".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-How&#95;Jerry&#95;14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-How_Jerry-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The site was a human-edited <a href="/wiki/Web_directory" title="Web directory">web directory</a>, organized in a hierarchy, as opposed to a searchable index of pages. In March 1994, "Jerry and David's Guide to the World Wide Web" was renamed "Yahoo!" and became known as the <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_Directory" title="Yahoo Directory">Yahoo Directory</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-How&#95;Jerry&#95;14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-How_Jerry-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Directory&#95;19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Directory-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The "yahoo.com" domain was registered on January 18, 1995.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Yahoo was incorporated on March 2, 1995. In 1995, a <a href="/wiki/Search_engine" title="Search engine">search engine</a> function, called Yahoo Search, was introduced. This allowed users to search Yahoo Directory.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Yahoo soon became the first popular online directory and search engine on the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Expansion_and_the_dot-com_bubble">Expansion and the dot-com bubble</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Countries_on_Yahoo.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Countries_on_Yahoo.svg/500px-Countries_on_Yahoo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="340" height="173" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Countries_on_Yahoo.svg/960px-Countries_on_Yahoo.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="2754" data-file-height="1398" /></a><figcaption>Map showing localized versions of Yahoo web portals, as of 2023</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo!_(4855962154).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Yahoo%21_%284855962154%29.jpg/250px-Yahoo%21_%284855962154%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="284" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Yahoo%21_%284855962154%29.jpg/330px-Yahoo%21_%284855962154%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Yahoo%21_%284855962154%29.jpg/500px-Yahoo%21_%284855962154%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3872" /></a><figcaption>Yahoo sign at <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a>, 2010</figcaption></figure>
<p>Yahoo grew rapidly throughout the 1990s. Yahoo became a <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public company</a> via an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> in April 1996 and its stock price rose 600% within two years.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto&#95;25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Like many search engines and web directories, Yahoo added a web portal, putting it in competition with services including <a href="/wiki/Excite_(web_portal)" title="Excite (web portal)">Excite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lycos" title="Lycos">Lycos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/America_Online" class="mw-redirect" title="America Online">America Online</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By 1998, Yahoo was the most popular starting point for web users,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the human-edited Yahoo Directory the most popular search engine,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Directory&#95;19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Directory-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> receiving 95 million page views per day, triple that of rival Excite.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto&#95;25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It also made many high-profile acquisitions. Yahoo began offering free <a href="/wiki/E-mail" class="mw-redirect" title="E-mail">e-mail</a> from October 1997 after the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/RocketMail" title="RocketMail">RocketMail</a>, which was then renamed to Yahoo Mail.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1998, Yahoo replaced <a href="/wiki/AltaVista" title="AltaVista">AltaVista</a> as the crawler-based search engine underlying the Directory with <a href="/wiki/Inktomi" title="Inktomi">Inktomi</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Yahoo's two biggest acquisitions were made in 1999: <a href="/wiki/GeoCities" title="GeoCities">GeoCities</a> for $3.6 billion<sup id="cite&#95;ref-buysgeo&#95;30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buysgeo-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Broadcast.com" title="Broadcast.com">Broadcast.com</a> for $5.7 billion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Its stock price skyrocketed during the <a href="/wiki/Dot-com_bubble" title="Dot-com bubble">dot-com bubble</a>, closing at an all-time high of $118.75/share on January 3, 2000. However, after the dot-com bubble burst, it reached a post-bubble low of $8.11 on September 26, 2001.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Missed_opportunities_to_acquire_Google">Missed opportunities to acquire Google</h4></div>
<p>Yahoo had two opportunities to acquire <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> that it did not pursue. In 1998, Google's founders <a href="/wiki/Larry_Page" title="Larry Page">Larry Page</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Brin" title="Sergey Brin">Sergey Brin</a> approached Yahoo to sell their nascent search engine for $1 million, but Yahoo declined the offer.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BusInsiderGoogle&#95;33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BusInsiderGoogle-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-EconTimesGoogle&#95;34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EconTimesGoogle-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A more significant opportunity arose in 2002, when Yahoo's then-CEO, <a href="/wiki/Terry_Semel" title="Terry Semel">Terry Semel</a>, entered into negotiations to purchase Google. Google was reportedly seeking a price of $5 billion. After weeks of negotiation, Yahoo's final offer was $3 billion, a figure that Google's leadership rejected, leading them to terminate the deal.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BusInsiderGoogle&#95;33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BusInsiderGoogle-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The failure to acquire Google in this second instance is widely considered one of the largest strategic errors in corporate history.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ForbesBlunder&#95;35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ForbesBlunder-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Yahoo began using <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> for search in June 2000.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Over the next four years, it developed its own search technologies, which it began using in 2004 partly using technology from its $280 million acquisition of Inktomi in 2002.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2003, Yahoo acquired <a href="/wiki/Overture_Services,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Overture Services, Inc.">Overture Services, Inc.</a> (formerly GoTo.com) for $1.63 billion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The deal was a strategic move to bolster its search advertising revenue in the face of growing competition from Google, as Overture was a pioneer in <a href="/wiki/Pay-per-click" title="Pay-per-click">pay-per-click</a> advertising.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In response to Google's <a href="/wiki/Gmail" title="Gmail">Gmail</a>, Yahoo began to offer unlimited email storage in 2007. In 2008, the company laid off hundreds of people as it struggled from competition.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Missed_opportunity_to_sell_to_Microsoft">Missed opportunity to sell to Microsoft</h4></div>
<p>In February 2008, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> made an unsolicited bid to acquire Yahoo Inc. for $44.6 billion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Feb-2008-425&#95;43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Feb-2008-425-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Yahoo Inc. rejected the bid, claiming that it "substantially undervalues" the company and was not in the interest of its shareholders. Although Microsoft increased its bid to $47 billion, Yahoo insisted on another 10%+ increase to the offer and Microsoft cancelled the offer in May 2008.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Yahoo!-Inc-May-2008-8-K&#95;45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-May-2008-8-K-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jun-2008-8-K&#95;46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jun-2008-8-K-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Decline,_sale,_and_post-acquisition_era"><span id="Decline.2C_sale.2C_and_post-acquisition_era"></span>Decline, sale, and post-acquisition era</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_data_breaches" title="Yahoo data breaches">Yahoo data breaches</a></div>
<p>In March 2004, Yahoo! launched a paid inclusion program whereby commercial websites were guaranteed listings on the Yahoo! <a href="/wiki/Web_search_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Web search engine">search engine</a> after payment.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This scheme was lucrative but proved unpopular both with website marketers (who were reluctant to pay), and the public (who were unhappy about the paid-for listings being indistinguishable from other search results).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of October 2006, Paid Inclusion ceased to guarantee any commercial listing and only helped the paid inclusion customers, by crawling their site more often and by providing some statistics on the searches that led to the page and some additional smart links (provided by customers as feeds) below the actual <a href="/wiki/URL" title="URL">URL</a>.
</p><p>In July 2009, after months of negotiation, Yahoo and Microsoft finalized a 10-year agreement known as the <b>Yahoo and Microsoft Search Alliance</b>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Under the terms of the alliance, Yahoo's websites would utilize Microsoft's <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Bing" title="Microsoft Bing">Bing</a> for algorithmic search results, while Yahoo's sales team became the exclusive sales force for both companies' premium search advertisers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The partnership required a complex migration of Yahoo's search technology and advertising platform to Microsoft's adCenter (later rebranded to Bing Ads), with the transition for advertisers and organic search results completed in October 2010.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Carol_Bartz" title="Carol Bartz">Carol Bartz</a>, former CEO of <a href="/wiki/Autodesk" title="Autodesk">Autodesk</a>, replaced Yang as CEO in January 2009.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jan-2009-8-K&#95;53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jan-2009-8-K-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In September 2011, she was fired by chairman Roy J. Bostock. The dismissal happened over the phone, a fact Bartz promptly communicated to employees in a widely publicized company-wide email.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> CFO Tim Morse was named as Interim CEO of the company.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Sep-2011-8-K&#95;55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Sep-2011-8-K-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2010, <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Groups" class="mw-redirect" title="Yahoo! Groups">Yahoo! Groups</a> started rolling out a major software change. This change was denounced by a vast majority of users.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
On September 29, 2010, Jim Stoneham, Vice President of Yahoo!'s Communities products, announced that based on members feedback, Yahoo! Groups would be rolling back the recent changes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>After the brief tenure of <a href="/wiki/Scott_Thompson_(businessman)" title="Scott Thompson (businessman)">Scott Thompson</a>, who was replaced on an interim basis by <a href="/wiki/Ross_Levinsohn" title="Ross Levinsohn">Ross Levinsohn</a>, Yahoo appointed <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> executive <a href="/wiki/Marissa_Mayer" title="Marissa Mayer">Marissa Mayer</a> as president and CEO, effective July 17, 2012.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2012-8-K&#95;59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2012-8-K-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Adware_and_spyware">Adware and spyware</h4></div>
<p>Yahoo! has funded <a href="/wiki/Spyware" title="Spyware">spyware</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adware" title="Adware">adware</a>—advertising from Yahoo!'s clients often appears on-screen in pop-ups generated from adware that a user may have installed on their computer without realizing it by accepting online offers to download software to fix computer clocks or improve computer security, add browser enhancements, etc. The frequency of advertising pop-ups for spyware, generated from a partnership with advertising distributor Walnut Ventures, who had a direct partnership with <a href="/wiki/Direct_Revenue" title="Direct Revenue">Direct Revenue</a>, could be increased or decreased based on Yahoo!'s immediate revenue needs, according to some former employees in Yahoo!'s sales department.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Work_in_the_People's_Republic_of_China"><span id="Work_in_the_People.27s_Republic_of_China"></span>Work in the People's Republic of China</h4></div>
<p>Yahoo!, along with <a href="/wiki/Google_China" title="Google China">Google China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_censorship_in_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Microsoft censorship in China">Microsoft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cisco" title="Cisco">Cisco</a>, <a href="/wiki/AOL" title="AOL">AOL</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skype_in_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Skype in China">Skype</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nortel" title="Nortel">Nortel</a> and others, has cooperated with the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party" title="Chinese Communist Party">Chinese Communist Party</a> in implementing a system of <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_in_China" title="Internet censorship in China">internet censorship in mainland China</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Unlike <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> or <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, which generally keep confidential records of its users outside <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a>, Yahoo! stated that the company cannot protect the privacy and confidentiality of its mainland Chinese customers from the authorities.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Critics say that the companies put profits before principles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a> state that it is "ironic that companies whose existence depends on freedom of information and expression have taken on the role of censor."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>In September 2005, Reporters Without Borders reported that in April 2005, <a href="/wiki/Shi_Tao_(journalist)" title="Shi Tao (journalist)">Shi Tao</a>, a journalist working for a Chinese newspaper, was sentenced to 10 years in prison by the <a href="/wiki/Changsha" title="Changsha">Changsha</a> Intermediate People's Court of <a href="/wiki/Hunan_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Hunan Province">Hunan Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (First trial case no. 29), for "providing state secrets to foreign entities". The "secrets" were a brief list of censorship orders he sent from a Yahoo! Mail account to the Asia <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">Democracy</a> Forum before the anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/1989_Tiananmen_Square_protests_and_massacre" title="1989 Tiananmen Square protests and massacre">1989 Tiananmen Square protests and massacre</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080801130828/http://www.rsf.org/IMG/pdf/Verdict_Shi_Tao.pdf">verdict as published by the Chinese government</a> stated that Shi Tao had sent the email through an anonymous Yahoo! account, that Yahoo! Holdings (the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> subsidiary of Yahoo) told the Chinese government that the IP address used to send the email was registered by the <a href="/wiki/Hunan" title="Hunan">Hunan</a> newspaper that Shi Tao worked for, and that police went straight to his offices and picked him up.
</p><p>In February 2006, Yahoo! General Counsel submitted a statement to the U.S. Congress in which Yahoo! denied knowing the true nature of the case against Shi Tao.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In April 2006, Yahoo! Holdings (Hong Kong) was investigated by Hong Kong's Privacy Commissioner for Personal Data.
</p><p>On 2 June 2006, the union representing journalists in the UK and Ireland (<a href="/wiki/National_Union_of_Journalists" title="National Union of Journalists">NUJ</a>) called on its 40,000 members to boycott all Yahoo! Inc. products and services to protest the Internet company's reported actions in China.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2007, evidence surfaced detailing the warrant which the Chinese authorities sent to Yahoo! officials, highlighting "State Secrets" as the charge against Shi Tao. The warrant requests to provide "all login times, corresponding IP addresses, and relevant email content from February 22, 2004, to present." for email ID "huoyan1989"<sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Analyst reports and human rights organizations have said that this evidence directly contradicts Yahoo!'s testimony before the U.S. Congress in February 2006.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Yahoo! contends it must respect the laws of governments in jurisdictions where it is operating.
</p><p>In February 2006, Reporters Without Borders released Chinese court documents stating that Yahoo! aided Chinese authorities in the case of <a href="/wiki/Dissident" title="Dissident">dissident</a> Li Zhi. In December 2003, Li Zhi was sentenced to 8 years imprisonment for "inciting <a href="/wiki/Subversion_(political)" class="mw-redirect" title="Subversion (political)">subversion</a>".
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Wang_Xiaoning" title="Wang Xiaoning">Wang Xiaoning</a> is a Chinese <a href="/wiki/Dissident" title="Dissident">dissident</a> from <a href="/wiki/Shenyang" title="Shenyang">Shenyang</a> who was arrested by authorities of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> for publishing controversial material online.
</p><p>In 2000 and 2001, Wang, who was an engineer by profession, posted electronic journals in a Yahoo! group calling for democratic reform and an end to single-party rule. He was arrested in September 2002 after Yahoo! assisted Chinese authorities by providing information. In September 2003, Wang was convicted of charges of "incitement to subvert state power" and sentenced to ten years in prison.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On April 18, 2007, Xiaoning's wife Yu Ling sued Yahoo! under human rights laws in federal court in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, United States.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Wang Xiaoning is named as a <a href="/wiki/Plaintiff" title="Plaintiff">plaintiff</a> in the Yahoo! suit, which was filed with help from the World Organization for Human Rights USA. "Yahoo! is guilty of 'an act of corporate irresponsibility,' said Morton Sklar, executive director of the group. "Yahoo! had reason to know that if they provided China with identification information that those individuals would be arrested."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-sue&#95;74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sue-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Yahoo!'s decision to assist China's authoritarian government came as part of a policy of reconciling its services with the Chinese government's policies. This came after China blocked Yahoo! services for a time. As reported in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> and many media sources:
</p>
<dl><dd>The suit says that in 2001, Wang was using a Yahoo! e-mail account to post anonymous writings to an Internet mailing list. The suit alleges that Yahoo!, under pressure from the Chinese government, blocked that account. Wang set up a new account via Yahoo! and began sending material again; the suit alleges that Yahoo! gave the government information that allowed it to identify and arrest Wang in September 2002. The suit says prosecutors in the Chinese courts cited Yahoo!'s cooperation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-sue&#95;74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sue-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>Human rights organizations groups are basing their case on a 217-year-old U.S. law to punish corporations for human rights violations abroad, an effort the Bush administration has opposed:
</p>
<dl><dd>In recent years, activists working with overseas plaintiffs have sued roughly two dozen businesses under the <a href="/wiki/Alien_Tort_Claims_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Alien Tort Claims Act">Alien Tort Claims Act</a>, which the activists say grants jurisdiction to American courts over acts abroad that violate international norms. Written by the <a href="/wiki/Founding_Fathers" class="mw-redirect" title="Founding Fathers">Founding Fathers</a> in 1789 for a different purpose, the law was rarely invoked until the 1980s.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-sue&#95;74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sue-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>On August 28, 2007, the World Organization for Human Rights sued Yahoo! for allegedly passing information (<a href="/wiki/Email" title="Email">email</a> and <a href="/wiki/IP_address" title="IP address">IP address</a>) with the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of the People&#39;s Republic of China">Chinese government</a> that caused the <a href="/wiki/Arrests" class="mw-redirect" title="Arrests">arrests</a> of writers and <a href="/wiki/Dissidents" class="mw-redirect" title="Dissidents">dissidents</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Lawsuit" title="Lawsuit">lawsuit</a> was filed in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> for <a href="/wiki/Journalists" class="mw-redirect" title="Journalists">journalists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shi_Tao_(journalist)" title="Shi Tao (journalist)">Shi Tao</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wang_Xiaoning" title="Wang Xiaoning">Wang Xiaoning</a>. Yahoo! stated that it supported <a href="/wiki/Privacy" title="Privacy">privacy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Free_expression" class="mw-redirect" title="Free expression">free expression</a> for it worked with other technology companies to solve <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> concerns.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On November 6, 2007, the US congressional panel criticised Yahoo! for not giving full details to the <a href="/wiki/House_Foreign_Affairs_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="House Foreign Affairs Committee">House Foreign Affairs Committee</a> the previous year, stating it had been "at best inexcusably negligent" and at worst "deceptive".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Closing_of_user-created_chat_rooms,_message_boards,_and_profiles_(2005)"><span id="Closing_of_user-created_chat_rooms.2C_message_boards.2C_and_profiles_.282005.29"></span>Closing of user-created chat rooms, message boards, and profiles (2005)</h4></div>
<p>As a result of media scrutiny relating to Internet child predators and a lack of significant ad revenues, Yahoo!'s "user created" chatrooms were closed down in June 2005.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Yahoo! News' message board section was closed December 19, 2006, due to the <a href="/wiki/Internet_troll" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet troll">trolling</a> phenomenon.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In addition, in mid-October 2008, Yahoo! deleted all information in millions of user profiles with no advance notice and little explanation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Image_search">Image search</h4></div>
<p>On May 25, 2006, a teacher who was intending to use the service with a class to search for "www", discovered that Yahoo!'s image search brought up sexually explicit images even when SafeSearch was on. Yahoo!'s response to this was, "Yahoo! is aware of this issue and is working to resolve it as quickly as possible".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Shark_fin_controversy">Shark fin controversy</h4></div>
<p>Yahoo Inc. previously owned a 14.95% stake in <a href="/wiki/Alibaba_Group" title="Alibaba Group">Alibaba</a>, which had been criticized for facilitating the sale of <a href="/wiki/Shark#Fishery" title="Shark">shark-derived products</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After investing in Alibaba, Yahoo! executives were asked about this issue, and responded: "We know the sale of shark products is both legal in Asia and a <a href="/wiki/Shark_fin_soup" title="Shark fin soup">centuries-old tradition</a>. This issue is largely a cultural-practices one."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  Alibaba would later ban the sale of shark fins on its platform in 2009.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="GeoCities_closure">GeoCities closure</h4></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/GeoCities" title="GeoCities">GeoCities</a> was a popular web hosting service founded in 1994. At the point Yahoo! purchased it in January 1999, it was reportedly the third most-browsed site on the World Wide Web.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-MarshallVNU&#95;84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarshallVNU-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Despite its popularity, it had still not become profitable by late 1998.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Ten years later Yahoo! closed Geocities,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> deleting millions of web pages in the process.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
In September 2009, a month before it was closed, GeoCities received 10,477,049 unique visitors.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Vijay Mukhi, an internet and cybersecurity expert quoted in the <i><a href="/wiki/Business_Standard" title="Business Standard">Business Standard</a></i>, criticized Yahoo's management of GeoCities; Mukhi described GeoCities as "a lost opportunity for Yahoo!", adding that "they could have made it a <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> if they wanted." <a href="/wiki/Rich_Skrenta" title="Rich Skrenta">Rich Skrenta</a>, the CEO of <a href="/wiki/Blekko" title="Blekko">Blekko</a>, posted on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" class="mw-redirect" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> an offer to take over GeoCities from Yahoo! in exchange for 50% future revenue share.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Tenure_of_Marissa_Mayer_(July_2012_-_June_2017)"><span id="Tenure_of_Marissa_Mayer_.28July_2012_-_June_2017.29"></span>Tenure of Marissa Mayer (July 2012 - June 2017)</h4></div>
<p>Upon her arrival, Mayer implemented several significant cultural and strategic changes. One of her first major policy decisions in 2013 was to revoke the company's remote work option, requiring all employees to work from the office to foster a more collaborative culture.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> She also initiated an aggressive acquisition strategy, purchasing over 50 startups, many of which were small, mobile-focused companies in an "acqui-hiring" approach to bring in new engineering talent.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Mayer's efforts to revitalize company culture included a controversial quarterly performance review (QPR) system implemented in 2013. The system required managers to rank employees on a bell curve, with those at the bottom often being terminated.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The policy was unpopular with many employees and led to a 2016 lawsuit from a former manager who alleged the system was used to conduct illegal mass layoffs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Despite some positive metrics, such as a temporary increase in website traffic in 2013,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the turnaround effort stalled. By January 2014, doubts about Mayer's progress emerged when she fired her high-profile COO hire, Henrique de Castro.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By December 2015, Mayer was facing intense criticism as performance declined.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In February 2016, Mayer announced layoffs amounting to 15% of the Yahoo workforce.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2009, Yahoo was criticized by the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Frontier_Foundation" title="Electronic Frontier Foundation">Electronic Frontier Foundation</a> for sending a <a href="/wiki/DMCA" class="mw-redirect" title="DMCA">DMCA</a> notice to <a href="/wiki/Whistleblower" class="mw-redirect" title="Whistleblower">whistleblower</a> website "<a href="/wiki/Cryptome" title="Cryptome">Cryptome</a>" for publicly posting details, prices, and procedures on obtaining <a href="/wiki/Personal_data" title="Personal data">personal data</a> of Yahoo's subscribers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2011, after some concerns over <a href="/wiki/Censorship" title="Censorship">censorship</a> of private emails regarding a website affiliated with <a href="/wiki/Occupy_Wall_Street" title="Occupy Wall Street">Occupy Wall Street</a> protests were raised, Yahoo responded with an apology and explained it as an accident.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-videosift.com&#95;101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-videosift.com-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-straight.com&#95;102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-straight.com-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On May 20, 2013, <a href="/wiki/Flickr" title="Flickr">Flickr</a>, Yahoo!'s image and video hosting website, unveiled a redesigned layout and additional features, including one <a href="/wiki/Terabyte" class="mw-redirect" title="Terabyte">terabyte</a> of free storage for all users, seamless photostream, cover photo and updated <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> App.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-CNET&#95;104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNET-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The redesigned layout fills the page with dynamically re-sized photos and, on the home page, displays recent comments on photos. <i>Tech Radar</i> described the new style Flickr as representing a "sea change" in its purpose.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many users criticized the changes, and the site's help forum received thousands of negative comments.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2014, a large scale malware attack was discovered by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fox_IT&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fox IT (page does not exist)">Fox IT</a> in the Netherlands that was targeted at <a href="/wiki/Java_(software_platform)" title="Java (software platform)">Java</a> and dated back to December 30, 2013, especially affecting users in Romania, France, and the UK and being delivered to 300,000 Yahoo! users per hour when they discovered it. Yahoo! was criticized for not providing any public guidance on the number of users affected or advice on what the affected users should do.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>
In October 2016, Scott Ard, a prominent editorial director fired from Yahoo in 2015,  filed a lawsuit accusing Mayer of leading a sexist campaign to purge male employees. Ard, a male employee, stated "Mayer encouraged and fostered the use of [an employee performance-rating system] to accommodate management's subjective biases and personal opinions, to the detriment of Yahoo's male employees". In the suit, Ard claimed that, prior to his firing, he had received "fully satisfactory" performance reviews since starting at the company in 2011 as head of editorial programming for Yahoo's home page, yet he was relieved of his role that was given to a woman who had been recently hired by Megan Lieberman, the editor-in-chief of Yahoo News.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-mercurynews.com&#95;110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mercurynews.com-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The lawsuit states:<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1244412712">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 32px}.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;margin-top:0}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{padding-left:1.6em}}</style></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Liberman stated that she was terminating [Ard] because she had not received a requested breakdown of [his] duties. [Ard] had already provided that very information as requested, however, and reminded Liberman that he had done so. Liberman's excuse for terminating [Ard] was a pretext.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-mercurynews.com&#95;110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mercurynews.com-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote><p> A second sexual discrimination lawsuit was filed separately by Gregory Anderson, who was fired in 2014, alleging the company's performance management system was arbitrary and unfair, making it the second sexism lawsuit Yahoo and Mayer faced in 2016.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Acquisitions_by_parent_company_Yahoo_Inc.">Acquisitions by parent company Yahoo Inc.</h4></div>
<p>In June 2013, Yahoo Inc. acquired <a href="/wiki/Blog" title="Blog">blogging</a> site <a href="/wiki/Tumblr" title="Tumblr">Tumblr</a> for $1.1 billion in cash.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jun-2013-8-K&#95;114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jun-2013-8-K-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Yahoo!-Inc-May-2013-8-K&#95;115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-May-2013-8-K-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> While the acquisition was intended to attract a younger audience, it failed to meet revenue targets. In 2016, Yahoo wrote down $712 million of Tumblr's value, acknowledging the acquisition had not paid off.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Verizon later sold Tumblr in 2019 for a fraction of its purchase price.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2014, Yahoo Inc. acquired <a href="/wiki/Cooliris" title="Cooliris">Cooliris</a>; it was subsequently shut down.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2014, Yahoo Inc. acquired <a href="/wiki/Video_advertising" title="Video advertising">video advertising</a> provider <a href="/wiki/BrightRoll" title="BrightRoll">BrightRoll</a> for $583 million; it was subsequently consolidated into Yahoo and AOL.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Feb-2015-10-K&#95;119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Feb-2015-10-K-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Sale_to_Verizon">Sale to Verizon</h4></div>
<p>On July 25, 2016, <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Communications" class="mw-redirect" title="Verizon Communications">Verizon Communications</a> announced the acquisition of Yahoo's core Internet business for $4.83 billion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2016-8-K&#95;120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2016-8-K-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The deal, which excluded Yahoo's stakes in <a href="/wiki/Alibaba_Group" title="Alibaba Group">Alibaba Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_Japan" title="Yahoo Japan">Yahoo Japan</a>, was delayed by the revelation of major data breaches.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Aug-2016-DEFA14A&#95;122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Aug-2016-DEFA14A-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2016-2-8-K&#95;123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2016-2-8-K-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On February 21, 2017, Verizon lowered its purchase price for Yahoo by $350 million and reached an agreement to share liabilities regarding the data breaches.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-bloomberg-lower&#95;124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg-lower-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-usatoday-verizonshaved&#95;125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday-verizonshaved-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On June 13, 2017, Verizon completed the acquisition and Marissa Mayer resigned.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Yahoo, AOL, and <a href="/wiki/HuffPost" title="HuffPost">HuffPost</a> were then combined under a new company, Oath Inc., later called <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Media" class="mw-redirect" title="Verizon Media">Verizon Media</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2017-8-K&#95;128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2017-8-K-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-verge-oath&#95;129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-oath-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The parts of the original Yahoo! Inc. not purchased by Verizon were renamed <a href="/wiki/Altaba" title="Altaba">Altaba</a> and liquidated in 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Post-Verizon_era">Post-Verizon era</h4></div>
<p>In September 2021, <a href="/wiki/Investment_fund" title="Investment fund">investment funds</a> managed by <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Global_Management" title="Apollo Global Management">Apollo Global Management</a> acquired 90% of Yahoo.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-owneragain&#95;131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-owneragain-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In November 2021, Yahoo announced that it was ending operations in mainland China due to the increasingly challenging business and legal environment.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2023, Yahoo announced plans to lay off 20% of its <a href="/wiki/Workforce" title="Workforce">workforce</a> (more than 1,600 employees) by the end of the year as part of a major restructuring of its ad tech division.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Following the acquisition by Apollo, CEO <a href="/wiki/Jim_Lanzone" title="Jim Lanzone">Jim Lanzone</a> initiated a strategy focused on a potential "turnaround", emphasizing the integration of <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a> across Yahoo's products.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This strategy included several key acquisitions, such as Commonstock in 2023 and the AI-driven news platform Artifact in 2024.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2026)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Illegal_access_of_user_accounts_by_former_Yahoo_engineer">Illegal access of user accounts by former Yahoo engineer</h4></div>
<p>In October 2019, a former Yahoo engineer, Reyes Daniel Ruiz, pleaded guilty to federal charges of illegally accessing user accounts. Ruiz had hacked about 6,000 users' accounts, including those of his friends, co-workers and many young women, seeking sexual images and videos.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Data_breaches">Data breaches</h4></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_data_breaches" title="Yahoo data breaches">Yahoo data breaches</a></div>
<p>The company reported two major <a href="/wiki/Data_breach" title="Data breach">data breaches</a> of user account data to <a href="/wiki/Security_hacker" title="Security hacker">hackers</a> during the second half of 2016. The first announced breach, reported in September 2016, had occurred sometime in late 2014, and affected over 500 million Yahoo! user accounts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-nyt1&#95;137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt1-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A separate data breach, occurring earlier around August 2013, was reported in December 2016, and affected over 1 billion user accounts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-nytimes&#95;dec2016&#95;138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes_dec2016-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Both breaches are considered the largest discovered in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Internet" title="History of the Internet">history of the Internet</a>. Specific details of material taken include names, email addresses, telephone numbers, encrypted or unencrypted security questions and answers, dates of birth, and <a href="/wiki/Encryption" title="Encryption">encrypted</a> <a href="/wiki/Password" title="Password">passwords</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BBC&#95;23&#95;Sept&#95;2016&#95;139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_23_Sept_2016-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Further, Yahoo! reported that the late 2014 breach likely used manufactured <a href="/wiki/HTTP_cookie" title="HTTP cookie">web cookies</a> to falsify login credentials, allowing hackers to gain access to any account without a password.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-wash1&#95;140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wash1-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-bbc2&#95;141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc2-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-wired&#95;dec2016&#95;142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wired_dec2016-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On September 22, 2016, Yahoo disclosed a <a href="/wiki/Data_breach" title="Data breach">data breach</a> that occurred in late 2014, in which information associated with at least 500 million user accounts,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> one of the largest breaches reported to date.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The United States indicted four men, including two employees of Russia's <a href="/wiki/Federal_Security_Service" title="Federal Security Service">Federal Security Service</a> (FSB), for their involvement in the hack.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On December 14, 2016, the company revealed that another separate data breach had occurred in 2014, with hackers obtaining sensitive account information, including security questions, to at least one billion accounts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The company stated that hackers had utilized stolen internal software to forge <a href="/wiki/HTTP_cookie" title="HTTP cookie">HTTP cookies</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On October 3, 2017, the company stated that all 3 billion of its user accounts were affected by the August 2013 theft.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Partners_and_sponsorships">Partners and sponsorships</h2></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:DUBLIN_PRIDE_2015_(_YAHOO!_WERE_THERE_-_WERE_YOU%3F)-106289_(19257385102).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/DUBLIN_PRIDE_2015_%28_YAHOO%21_WERE_THERE_-_WERE_YOU%3F%29-106289_%2819257385102%29.jpg/250px-DUBLIN_PRIDE_2015_%28_YAHOO%21_WERE_THERE_-_WERE_YOU%3F%29-106289_%2819257385102%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="184" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/DUBLIN_PRIDE_2015_%28_YAHOO%21_WERE_THERE_-_WERE_YOU%3F%29-106289_%2819257385102%29.jpg/500px-DUBLIN_PRIDE_2015_%28_YAHOO%21_WERE_THERE_-_WERE_YOU%3F%29-106289_%2819257385102%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="5423" data-file-height="4000" /></a><figcaption>The 2015 <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> LGBTQ Pride Festival, sponsored by Yahoo</figcaption></figure>
<p>On September 11, 2001, Yahoo announced its partnership with <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002 FIFA World Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a> tournaments. It was one of FIFA's 15 partners at the tournaments. The deal included co-branding the organization's websites.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Yahoo sponsored the <a href="/wiki/2012_Sundance_Film_Festival" title="2012 Sundance Film Festival">2012 Sundance Film Festival</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/NBC_Sports_Group" title="NBC Sports Group">NBC Sports Group</a> aligned with Yahoo Sports the same year with content and program offerings on mobile and desktop platforms.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NBC&#95;158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBC-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Yahoo announced television video partnerships in 2013 with <a href="/wiki/Cond%C3%A9_Nast" title="Condé Nast">Condé Nast</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Conde&#95;159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Conde-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">WWE</a>, <a href="/wiki/ABC_News_(United_States)" title="ABC News (United States)">ABC NEWS</a>, and <a href="/wiki/CNBC" title="CNBC">CNBC</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-2013partners&#95;160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013partners-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Yahoo entered into a 10-year collaboration in 2014, as a founding partner of <a href="/wiki/Levi%27s_Stadium" title="Levi&#39;s Stadium">Levi's Stadium</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_49ers" title="San Francisco 49ers">San Francisco 49ers</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Levi&#95;161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levi-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a> partnered with Yahoo Sports to stream games, offer virtual and augmented-reality fan experiences, and in 2018 <a href="/wiki/NBA_League_Pass" title="NBA League Pass">NBA League Pass</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NBA1&#95;162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBA1-162"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-NBA2&#95;163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBA2-163"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Yahoo Sportsbook launched in November 2019, a collaboration with BetMGM.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-sportsbook&#95;164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sportsbook-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Digi&#95;165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Digi-165"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/BuzzFeed" title="BuzzFeed">BuzzFeed</a> acquired <a href="/wiki/HuffPost" title="HuffPost">HuffPost</a> from Yahoo in November 2020, in a stock deal with Yahoo as a minority shareholder.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Buzz&#95;166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buzz-166"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>166<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Buzz1&#95;167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buzz1-167"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>167<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The NFL partnered with Yahoo in 2020, to introduce a new "Watch Together" function on the Yahoo Sports app for interactive co-viewing through a synchronized livestream of local and primetime NFL games.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-SBJ&#95;168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBJ-168"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Paley_Center_for_Media" title="Paley Center for Media">Paley Center for Media</a> collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_(2017%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Yahoo (2017–present)">Verizon Media</a> to exclusively stream programs on Yahoo platforms beginning in 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Paley&#95;169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paley-169"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Yahoo became the main sponsor for the <a href="/wiki/Pramac_Racing" title="Pramac Racing">Pramac Racing</a> team and the first title sponsor for the 2021 ESport/MotoGP Championship season.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>170<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Yahoo, the official partner for the September 2021 <a href="/wiki/New_York_Fashion_Week" title="New York Fashion Week">New York Fashion Week</a> event also unveiled sponsorship for the <a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Minkoff" class="mw-redirect" title="Rebecca Minkoff">Rebecca Minkoff</a> collection via a <a href="/wiki/NFT" class="mw-redirect" title="NFT">NFT</a> space.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NYFW&#95;171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYFW-171"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In September 2021, it was announced that Yahoo partnered with <a href="/wiki/Shopify" title="Shopify">Shopify</a>, connecting the e-commerce merchants on Yahoo Finance, AOL and elsewhere.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Shopify&#95;172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shopify-172"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>172<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
